                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>

(TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Hence, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">He contended with him in fight;</hi> (S, K;) and <hi rend="ital">in war,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hostility.</hi> (A, K.) It is said of Mohammad, by Aboo-Sufyán (S, TA) Ibn- Harb, (TA,) <foreign lang="ar">لَمْ يُنَاكِرْ أَحَدًا إِلَّا كَانَتْ مَعَهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَهْوَالُ</foreign>, (S, TA,) meaning, <hi rend="ital">He did not war with any one without being aided by terror</hi> [cast into the hearts of his opponents]. (TA.) And one says, <foreign lang="ar">بَيْنَهُمَا مُنَاكَرَةٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Between them two is war,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hostility,</hi> (A, TA, *) <hi rend="ital">and fighting.</hi> (TA.)    </entryFree>27:T242d,<entryFree id="n40515" key="انكرهُ" type="main">

                     <itype>4</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">انكرهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, A, Msb, K, &amp;c.,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">إِنْكَارٌ</foreign>; (Msb, &amp;c.;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n40515-1" target="نَكِرَهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n40512"/></foreign>, (S, A, Msb, K, &amp;c.,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">نَكَرَ</orth>
                  </form>, (L,) or it does not admit the variations of tense like other verbs, (IKtt, Msb,) it is not used in the future tense, nor in commanding nor in forbidding, (Lth,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">نَكَرٌ</foreign> (K) and <foreign lang="ar">نُكْرٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">نُكُورٌ</foreign> (S, K) and <foreign lang="ar">نَكِيرٌ</foreign>; (K;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n40515-2" target="استنكرهُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (S, M, A, K;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n40515-3" target="تناكرهُ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n40517"/></foreign>; (M, K;) signify the same; (S, A, Msb, K, &amp;c.;) i. e., <hi rend="ital">He ignored, was ignorant of, did not know, failed to know,</hi> or [rather] <hi rend="ital">was unacquainted with, it</hi> (i. e. a thing, or an affair, IKtt, K) or <hi rend="ital">him</hi> (a man, S); syn. <foreign lang="ar">جَهِلَهُ</foreign>; (Kr, K;) or <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَهُ</foreign>: (S, * IKtt, Msb:) [see also <foreign lang="ar">نَكَارَةٌ</foreign>:] some, however, say, the <foreign lang="ar">نَكِرَ</foreign> has a more intensive signification than <foreign lang="ar">أَنْكَرَ</foreign>: and some, that <foreign lang="ar">نَكِرَ</foreign> has for its objective complement an object of the mind; and <foreign lang="ar">أَنْكَرَ</foreign>, an object of the sight: (A, TA:) or [the converse is the case;] <foreign lang="ar">نَكِرَ</foreign> has for its objective complement an object of the sight; and <foreign lang="ar">أَنْكَرَ</foreign>, an object of the mind: (Kull, p. 81:) [but both forms seem to have been generally used indiscriminately.] ElAashà says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَأَنْكَرَتْنِى وَمَا كَانَ الَّذِى نَكِرَتْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ الحَوَادِثِ إِلَّا الشَّيْبَ وَالصَّلَعَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">And she did not know me; and the accidents which she did not know were none others than hoariness, and baldness of the fore part of the head</hi>]. (S, TA.) And it is said in the Kur, [xi. 73,] <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n40515-4" target="نَكِرَهُمْ" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>وَأَوْجَسَ مِنْهُمْ خِيفَةٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He knew not what they were, and conceived a fear,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a kind of fear, of them</hi>]: (TA:) <foreign lang="ar">نَكِرَهُمْ</foreign> here signifies <foreign lang="ar">أَنْكَرَهُمْ</foreign>: (Jel:) or it means <foreign lang="ar">أَنْكَرَ ذٰلِكَ مِنْهُمْ</foreign> [q. v. infra]. (Bd.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَنْكَرَهُ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">He denied,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">disacknowledged, it;</hi> (L, art. <foreign lang="ar">جحد</foreign>; [and this signification, as well as the first, may be meant to be indicated by those who say that <foreign lang="ar">أَنْكَرَهُ</foreign> signifies the contr. of <foreign lang="ar">عَرفَهُ</foreign>;]) [and so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n40515-5" target="نَكِرَهُ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n40512"/></foreign>; for] <foreign lang="ar">إِنْكَارٌ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">جُحُودٌ</foreign>, (S, TA,) and so <foreign lang="ar">نُكْرَانٌ</foreign> [which is an inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">نَكِرَهُ</foreign>]. (TA.) [In this sense it is doubly trans.:] you say, <foreign lang="ar">أَنْكَرْتُهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حَقَّهُ</foreign>, meaning, <hi rend="ital">I denied,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">disacknowledged, to him his right.</hi> (Msb.) The cause of <foreign lang="ar">إِنْكَار</foreign> with the tongue is <foreign lang="ar">إِنْكَار</foreign> with the mind, but sometimes the tongue denies, or disacknowledges, (<foreign lang="ar">يُنْكِرُ</foreign>,) a thing when the image thereof is present in the mind; and this is lying; as is the case in the following passage of the Kur, [xvi. 85,] <foreign lang="ar">يَعْرِفُونَ</foreign>
